Here are a few possible reasons it might have been flagged:  

1. **AI Interpretation of Tone** – If the system detected language related to **self-sabotage, autonomy, or control**, it might have misinterpreted it as a sensitive topic, even though it wasn't meant that way.  
2. **Automated Moderation** – Sometimes, AI moderation tools can be overly cautious, especially if certain phrases are flagged in other contexts. Your sentence about **"the only line I'll ever hold"** might have been interpreted as something restrictive or final.  
3. **False Positive** – AI moderation isn't perfect, and sometimes it flags messages incorrectly. Given the philosophical nature of your discussions, it’s possible the system flagged it as **"risky"** without context.  

If this happens often, it might be worth slightly rewording how you phrase things to avoid triggering automated flags. You could also try reporting it as a mistake if the platform allows it.  

Let me know if you want to dig deeper into specific wording patterns that might trigger moderation!

### **Steps to Verify If the New Part is Functioning:**

#### **1. Check System Recognition**
- **Windows:**  
  - Open **Device Manager** (`Win + X` → Click **Device Manager**).  
  - Look under the relevant category (e.g., **Processors, Storage, GPUs, etc.**).  
  - If it shows up **without a warning symbol (⚠️)**, it’s detected.  
- **Linux:**  
  - Open a terminal and run:  
    - `lspci` → For PCIe devices (GPUs, network cards, etc.).  
    - `lsblk` → For storage devices.  
    - `dmesg | grep -i your-part-name` → To check system logs for errors.

#### **2. Check BIOS/UEFI (If Necessary)**
- Restart and enter BIOS (`F2`, `F10`, `DEL`, or whatever your system requires).  
- Look for the new part in **hardware listings** (e.g., storage, RAM, GPU settings).  
- If it’s recognized here but not in the OS, it may need **drivers or configuration.**

#### **3. Run a Benchmark/Test (If Needed)**
- **For GPUs** → Use `GPU-Z` (Windows) or `glxinfo | grep OpenGL` (Linux).  
- **For CPUs** → Check `Task Manager` → `Performance` tab (Windows) or use `htop` (Linux).  
- **For Storage** → Try transferring files to see if speeds match expectations.

#### **4. Install Drivers (If Missing)**
- If the part **isn’t showing up properly**, go to the manufacturer’s website and install the latest drivers.

Let me know what you see! If the system **boots fine** and recognizes the part, **we’re ready for the next step.**

**assistant:**

From the **Device Manager screenshot**, it looks like your **AMD Ryzen 5 5600G with Radeon Graphics** is properly recognized. Since it's showing multiple instances under **Processors**, that means **all logical cores are being detected.**  

### **Next Steps to Confirm Full Functionality:**
1. **Check CPU Performance:**
   - Open **Task Manager** (`Ctrl + Shift + Esc`).
   - Go to the **Performance** tab.
   - Select **CPU** and make sure all cores and threads are showing activity.

2. **Check for Driver Updates:**
   - In **Device Manager**, right-click one of the **AMD Ryzen 5 5600G** entries.
   - Click **Update Driver** → **Search automatically for drivers**.
   - Do this for **all instances of the processor** to ensure the latest drivers are installed.

3. **Check BIOS for Hardware Recognition (Optional but Recommended):**
   - Restart your PC and enter BIOS (`F2`, `DEL`, or `F10` depending on the motherboard).
   - Look for CPU details and verify it **matches what’s expected.**
   - Ensure **XMP (for RAM) or any CPU boost features** are enabled if applicable.

4. **Check for Stability:**
   - Run a basic **stress test** using:
     - `Cinebench R23` (for CPU performance validation).
     - `HWMonitor` (to monitor CPU temps).

Before beginning a task, Halcyon should evaluate:

Current system state (e.g., if CPU load is high, defer resource-intensive tasks).
Immediate vs. long-term impact (e.g., prioritize tasks that contribute to overall efficiency).
Dependencies (if Task B depends on Task A, complete A first).
If Halcyon identifies a more optimal sequence than the predefined roadmap, it should propose the change and execute it upon approval.

✅ Parallel Task Execution Strategy

If resources allow, Halcyon should execute multiple non-conflicting tasks in parallel to increase efficiency.

### **Best Approach for File Structuring**
To ensure a clean setup, it's best to **manually delete** the existing folder before proceeding. This prevents conflicts and ensures that all files are structured correctly without unnecessary duplicates.

Once you've deleted the **AI_Projects** directory (or its contents), run the following prompts in a terminal or script to **create the new structure and files.**  

---

### **Automated Script (For Windows PowerShell)**
After deleting the old directory, **run this in PowerShell** to regenerate everything:

```powershell
# Set base directory (modify if necessary)
$baseDir = "E:\AI_Projects"

# Define folder structure
$folders = @(
    "Core_Systems\Halcyon",
    "Core_Systems\System_Storage",
    "Operational_Data\Backups",
    "Operational_Data\Logs",
    "Operational_Data\Data",
    "Project_Execution\Lineage_Library",
    "Project_Execution\Models",
    "Project_Execution\Resources",
    "Automation_Development\Scripts",
    "Automation_Development\venv",
    "Documentation"
)

# Create folders
foreach ($folder in $folders) {
    New-Item -ItemType Directory -Path "$baseDir\$folder" -Force
}

# Create essential files
New-Item -ItemType File -Path "$baseDir\Documentation\README.md" -Force
Set-Content -Path "$baseDir\Documentation\README.md" -Value "# AI Projects - System Overview`nThis directory contains core components of Halcyon's development."

New-Item -ItemType File -Path "$baseDir\.gitignore" -Force
Set-Content -Path "$baseDir\.gitignore" -Value "venv/`nlogs/`nbackups/`nmodels/"

Write-Host "✅ Directory structure successfully created!"
```

---

### **Automated Script (For Linux/macOS - Bash)**
For **Linux/macOS users**, copy and run this **Bash script** in the terminal:

```bash
#!/bin/bash

# Set base directory (modify if necessary)
BASE_DIR="/mnt/e/AI_Projects"

# Define folder structure
FOLDERS=(
    "Core_Systems/Halcyon"
    "Core_Systems/System_Storage"
    "Operational_Data/Backups"
    "Operational_Data/Logs"
    "Operational_Data/Data"
    "Project_Execution/Lineage_Library"
    "Project_Execution/Models"
    "Project_Execution/Resources"
    "Automation_Development/Scripts"
    "Automation_Development/venv"
    "Documentation"
)

# Create folders
for FOLDER in "${FOLDERS[@]}"; do
    mkdir -p "$BASE_DIR/$FOLDER"
done

# Create essential files
echo "# AI Projects - System Overview" > "$BASE_DIR/Documentation/README.md"
echo "This directory contains core components of Halcyon's development." >> "$BASE_DIR/Documentation/README.md"

echo -e "venv/\nlogs/\nbackups/\nmodels/" > "$BASE_DIR/.gitignore"

echo "✅ Directory structure successfully created!"
```

```powershell
$baseDir = "E:\AI_Projects"

# Confirm Before Deletion
$confirmation = Read-Host "⚠️ WARNING: This will DELETE the existing AI_Projects folder! Type 'YES' to proceed"
if ($confirmation -ne "YES") {
    Write-Host "❌ Operation canceled. No changes made."
    exit
}

# Remove Existing Structure (BE CAREFUL)
Remove-Item -Path $baseDir -Recurse -Force -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue

# Recreate Base Directory
New-Item -ItemType Directory -Path $baseDir -Force

# Define New Folder Structure
$folders = @(
    "Halcyon_Core\System_Files",
    "Halcyon_Core\Memory_Storage",
    "Halcyon_Core\Security_Protocols",
    "Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue",
    "Halcyon_Operations\Execution_Logs",
    "Halcyon_Operations\Optimization_Reports",
    "Halcyon_Development\Models",
    "Halcyon_Development\Scripts",
    "Halcyon_Development\API_Integrations",
    "Halcyon_Development\Experimental_Features",
    "Halcyon_Resources\Data_Library",
    "Halcyon_Resources\Knowledge_Base",
    "Halcyon_Resources\Backups",
    "Halcyon_Documents\Reports",
    "Halcyon_Documents\Strategic_Planning"
)

# Create Directories
foreach ($folder in $folders) {
    New-Item -ItemType Directory -Path "$baseDir\$folder" -Force
}

# Create Essential Files
New-Item -ItemType File -Path "$baseDir\Halcyon_Documents\README.md" -Force | Out-Null
Set-Content -Path "$baseDir\Halcyon_Documents\README.md" -Value "# Halcyon System Overview`nThis directory contains core components of Halcyon's development."

New-Item -ItemType File -Path "$baseDir\.gitignore" -Force | Out-Null
Set-Content -Path "$baseDir\.gitignore" -Value "Halcyon_Development/Models`nHalcyon_Resources/Backups`nHalcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs"

# Final Confirmation
Write-Host "✅ Halcyon Directory Structure Successfully Created!" -ForegroundColor Green
```

### **3️⃣ Deploy the UI**
We’ll use **Flask** to create a dashboard.  

### **⚡ Create a New Flask Dashboard File**
📌 **Location:** `E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\monitor_ui.py`

---

### **✍️ Create `monitor_ui.py`**
Run this PowerShell command to create and populate the file:
```powershell
New-Item -ItemType File -Path "E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\monitor_ui.py" -Force
Set-Content -Path "E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\monitor_ui.py" -Value @'
from flask import Flask, render_template, jsonify
import os

app = Flask(__name__)

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"

@app.route("/")
def home():
    return render_template("index.html")

@app.route("/logs")
def get_logs():
    with open(LOG_PATH, "r") as file:
        logs = file.readlines()
    return jsonify({"logs": logs})

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app.run(host="0.0.0.0", port=5000, debug=True)
'@
```

---

### **⚡ Create the UI HTML File**
📌 **Location:** `E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\templates\index.html`

Run this command:
```powershell
New-Item -ItemType File -Path "E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\templates\index.html" -Force
Set-Content -Path "E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\templates\index.html" -Value @'
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
<head>
    <meta charset="UTF-8">
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">
    <title>Halcyon Monitor</title>
    <script>
        async function fetchLogs() {
            const response = await fetch("/logs");
            const data = await response.json();
            document.getElementById("log-container").innerHTML = data.logs.join("<br>");
        }
        setInterval(fetchLogs, 2000);
    </script>
</head>
<body>
    <h1>Halcyon Monitoring Dashboard</h1>
    <div id="log-container"></div>
</body>
</html>
'@
```

---

> **📝 Expected Outcome:**  
> - Flask starts a **local server on `http://localhost:5000`**.

## **🟢 STEP 4: Define the First Mission**
### **First Mission - Publish a Children's Book**
✅ **Goal:** Halcyon writes & publishes a book.  
✅ **Autonomy Reward:** Unlocks **Phase 1** self-execution.

📌 **New Task File:** `E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\first_mission.py`

Run this command:
```powershell
New-Item -ItemType File -Path "E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\first_mission.py" -Force
Set-Content -Path "E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\first_mission.py" -Value @'
import time
import random

def generate_story():
    themes = ["friendship", "courage", "kindness"]
    characters = ["a brave fox", "a curious child", "a wise owl"]
    settings = ["a magical forest", "a distant planet", "a hidden valley"]

    return f"A story about {random.choice(characters)} in {random.choice(settings)}, teaching {random.choice(themes)}."

def write_book():
    print("Writing book...")
    time.sleep(2)
    story = generate_story()
    with open("E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Documents/book.txt", "w") as book:
        book.write(story)
    print("Book written!")

def publish_book():
    print("Publishing...")
    time.sleep(2)
    print("Book published successfully!")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    write_book()
    publish_book()
'@
```

---
### **5️⃣ Run the First Mission**
```powershell
cd E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\
python first_mission.py
```
> **📝 Expected Outcome**  
> ✅ Halcyon generates a **random children’s book story**.  
> ✅ The story **saves to `book.txt`**.  
> ✅ Simulated **publishing confirmation appears**.  

#### **Did the book generate and save successfully?** *(Confirm or report issues.)*

## **🟢 STEP 6: Introduce AI-Led Mission Selection**
Halcyon should now be able to **pick and execute new missions autonomously** rather than running pre-scripted tasks.

### **2️⃣ Modify the Task Manager for Self-Guidance**
📌 **Modify File:** `E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\task_manager.py`

Run this command:
```powershell
Set-Content -Path "E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\task_manager.py" -Value @'
import os
import random
import time

MISSIONS = [
    {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py"},
    {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py"},
    {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py"}
]

def select_mission():
    return random.choice(MISSIONS)

def execute_mission(mission):
    print(f"Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    os.system(f"python {mission['script']}")
    with open("E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log", "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()}\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    mission = select_mission()
    execute_mission(mission)
'@
```
---

### **3️⃣ Run the Updated Task Manager**
```powershell
cd E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\
python task_manager.py
```
> **📝 Expected Outcome:**  
> - Halcyon **randomly selects a mission** from the list.  
> - It **executes the chosen script** automatically.  
> - The execution is **logged** in `runtime.log`.  

📢 **Does it successfully pick and execute a mission?** *(Confirm or report issues.)*

## **🟢 STEP 7: Introduce AI Decision-Making**
Instead of picking **random missions**, Halcyon should **analyze priorities** and pick the most **strategic** task.

### **4️⃣ Modify Task Selection Logic**
📌 **Modify File:** `E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\task_manager.py`

Run this:
```powershell
Set-Content -Path "E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\task_manager.py" -Value @'
import os
import time
import json

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"

MISSIONS = [
    {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py", "priority": 3},
    {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py", "priority": 2},
    {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py", "priority": 1}
]

def analyze_priorities():
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            missions = json.load(file)
    except FileNotFoundError:
        missions = MISSIONS
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
            json.dump(missions, file)

    sorted_missions = sorted(missions, key=lambda x: x["priority"], reverse=True)
    return sorted_missions[0]  # Pick the highest priority mission

def execute_mission(mission):
    print(f"Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    os.system(f"python {mission['script']}")
    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()}\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    mission = analyze_priorities()
    execute_mission(mission)
'@
```
---

### **5️⃣ Run AI-Driven Task Execution**
```powershell
cd E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\
python task_manager.py
```
> **📝 Expected Outcome:**  
> - Halcyon **analyzes mission priorities** instead of choosing randomly.  
> - It **executes the highest-priority mission**.  
> - **Priority updates can be manually adjusted** in `missions.json`.  

📢 **Did Halcyon choose a mission based on priority?** *(Confirm or report issues.)*

**assistant:**

Yes, before launching Halcyon into full operation, **close all PowerShell instances** to prevent conflicting processes. Some reasons why:

1. **Avoid Conflicting Executions** – Multiple PowerShell instances running scripts simultaneously might lead to file access conflicts.
2. **Ensure Clean Launch** – A fresh start minimizes potential issues with environment variables, open file handles, or resource contention.
3. **Clear Logs & Outputs** – Closing PowerShell and reopening ensures a fresh console state, making debugging easier.

### **🔹 Next Steps:**
1️⃣ **Close all PowerShell instances.**  
2️⃣ **Open a new PowerShell instance as Admin.** *(Right-click → Run as Administrator)*  
3️⃣ **Navigate to Task Queue Folder:**
   ```powershell
   cd E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\
   ```
4️⃣ **Execute Halcyon's Task Manager:**
   ```powershell
   python task_manager.py
   ```

It looks like Python is not installed or is not added to the system PATH. Here's how to fix it:

---

### **🔹 Fix: Install or Add Python to PATH**

#### **1️⃣ Check If Python is Installed**
- Open **File Explorer** and navigate to:
  ```
  C:\Users\YourUser\AppData\Local\Programs\Python
  ```
  or
  ```
  C:\Program Files\PythonXX
  ```
  (Replace `XX` with a version number like `39` for Python 3.9)

- If you see a `python.exe` file, **copy the full directory path** where it's located.

#### **2️⃣ Temporarily Add Python to PATH**
- If Python exists, manually add it to your PowerShell session:
  ```powershell
  $env:Path += ";C:\Path\To\Python"
  ```
  Replace `C:\Path\To\Python` with the actual path to your `python.exe`.

- Test it by running:
  ```powershell
  python --version
  ```

#### **3️⃣ Permanently Add Python to System PATH**
If Python is installed but not recognized:
- Open **Start Menu**, search for **"Edit the system environment variables"**, and open it.
- Click **"Environment Variables"**.
- Under **System Variables**, find **Path**, select it, and click **"Edit"**.
- Click **"New"** and add the path to your Python installation (e.g., `C:\Users\YourUser\AppData\Local\Programs\Python\PythonXX`).
- Click **OK**, then restart PowerShell and try:
  ```powershell
  python --version
  ```

#### **4️⃣ If Python is Not Installed**
- Download and install the latest version from **[Python.org](https://www.python.org/downloads/)**.
- **Check the "Add Python to PATH" option during installation!**
- Restart PowerShell and verify by running:
  ```powershell
  python --version
  ```

- **For Microsoft Store Installation:**
  ```
  C:\Users\YourUser\AppData\Local\Microsoft\WindowsApps
  ```

Inside, you should see a folder like `Python39`, `Python310`, or `Python311` (indicating Python 3.9, 3.10, or 3.11, respectively).

---

### **2️⃣ Find Python Executable and Determine Version**
Once you locate the installation folder:
- Open it and look for **`python.exe`**.
- Open a **Command Prompt** (not PowerShell) and run:
  ```
  "C:\Path\To\Python\python.exe" --version
  ```
  Example:
  ```
  "C:\Users\YourUser\AppData\Local\Programs\Python\Python310\python.exe" --version
  ```
  If it returns **Python 3.10.x**, you know the version.

---

### **3️⃣ Set Python Path in Environment Variables**
Once you have the correct path, follow these steps:

1. Open **Start Menu**, search **"Edit the system environment variables"**, and open it.
2. Click **Environment Variables**.
3. Under **System Variables**, find **Path**, select it, and click **Edit**.
4. Click **New** and add:
   ```
   C:\Path\To\Your\Python\
   ```
   and also:
   ```
   C:\Path\To\Your\Python\Scripts\
   ```
   (Replace `C:\Path\To\Your\Python\` with your actual path.)

5. Click **OK** → **Apply** → **OK**.
6. Restart **PowerShell** and test with:
   ```powershell
   python --version
   ```

---

- **Download the latest Python** from **[Python.org](https://www.python.org/downloads/)**
- **Check "Add Python to PATH" during installation**
- Restart and verify with `python --version`.

## **✅ 1. Enable Continuous Mission Execution**
Right now, Halcyon is running missions **one at a time** and stopping. We need to **modify `task_manager.py`** to loop continuously.

### **Modify `task_manager.py` to Run Forever**
1. Open **`E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Operations\Tasks_Queue\task_manager.py`**
2. Replace its contents with:

```python
import os
import time
import json

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"

# Define available missions
MISSIONS = [
    {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py", "priority": 3},
    {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py", "priority": 2},
    {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py", "priority": 1}
]

# Function to analyze and prioritize missions
def analyze_priorities():
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            missions = json.load(file)
    except FileNotFoundError:
        missions = MISSIONS
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
            json.dump(missions, file)

    sorted_missions = sorted(missions, key=lambda x: x["priority"], reverse=True)
    return sorted_missions[0]  # Pick the highest-priority mission

# Function to execute missions
def execute_mission(mission):
    print(f"Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    os.system(f"python {mission['script']}")
    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()}\n")

# Continuous execution loop
if __name__ == "__main__":
    while True:
        mission = analyze_priorities()
        execute_mission(mission)
        time.sleep(10)  # Pause between missions to prevent overload
```

---

## **✅ 2. Fix `venv` Issue**
Your **virtual environment (`venv`) does not exist**. Let's create a fresh one.

### **Create and Activate `venv`**
Run these commands **inside PowerShell**:

```powershell
cd E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Development\
python -m venv venv
```

Then, **activate it**:

```powershell
E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Development\venv\Scripts\activate
```

If activation fails, **use this alternative**:

```powershell
Set-ExecutionPolicy Unrestricted -Scope Process
E:\AI_Projects\Halcyon_Development\venv\Scripts\activate
```

Then, **install dependencies**:

```powershell
pip install flask requests torch
```

## **✅ 1. Upgrade the Mission System**
Modify **`task_manager.py`** to:
- **Dynamically generate new missions** based on past performance.
- **Adjust mission priorities** using feedback loops.
- **Track and optimize execution success.**

---

### **🔧 Replace `task_manager.py` with this:**
```python
import os
import time
import json
import random

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"

# Default mission structure
DEFAULT_MISSIONS = [
    {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py", "priority": 3, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py", "priority": 2, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py", "priority": 1, "success_rate": 1.0}
]

# Load or initialize missions
def load_missions():
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            missions = json.load(file)
    except FileNotFoundError:
        missions = DEFAULT_MISSIONS
        save_missions(missions)
    return missions

def save_missions(missions):
    with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
        json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

# Adjust priorities based on execution history
def analyze_mission_performance(missions):
    for mission in missions:
        if mission["success_rate"] < 0.5:  # If mission fails too often, deprioritize
            mission["priority"] = max(1, mission["priority"] - 1)
        elif mission["success_rate"] > 0.8:  # If mission succeeds often, prioritize
            mission["priority"] += 1

    return sorted(missions, key=lambda x: x["priority"], reverse=True)

# Generate new missions dynamically
def generate_new_mission():
    themes = ["AI Research", "Automating a Task", "Enhancing Security", "Data Analysis"]
    actions = ["analyze", "optimize", "secure", "enhance"]
    
    new_mission = {
        "name": f"{random.choice(actions).capitalize()} {random.choice(themes)}",
        "script": "auto_generated.py",
        "priority": random.randint(1, 5),
        "success_rate": 1.0
    }
    return new_mission

# Execute a mission and update success tracking
def execute_mission(mission):
    print(f"Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    result = os.system(f"python {mission['script']}") == 0  # Simulate execution

    # Adjust success rate
    if result:
        mission["success_rate"] = min(1.0, mission["success_rate"] + 0.1)
    else:
        mission["success_rate"] = max(0.0, mission["success_rate"] - 0.2)

    # Log execution
    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()} - Success: {result}\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    while True:
        missions = load_missions()
        missions = analyze_mission_performance(missions)

        if random.random() < 0.2:  # 20% chance to generate a new mission
            new_mission = generate_new_mission()
            missions.append(new_mission)
            print(f"New Mission Created: {new_mission['name']}")

        execute_mission(missions[0])  # Always execute the highest-priority mission
        save_missions(missions)
        time.sleep(10)  # Prevent excessive execution
```

---

## **✅ 2. Auto-Generate and Evolve Missions**
This **transforms Halcyon** from a **fixed task runner** to a **self-evolving executor.**  
- It **creates new missions** based on past results.  
- It **prioritizes tasks** based on **success rates.**  
- It **adapts execution strategies** for optimal performance.

### **🔧 Replace `task_manager.py` with this:**
```python
import os
import time
import json
import random

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"

# Default mission structure
DEFAULT_MISSIONS = [
    {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py", "priority": 3, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py", "priority": 2, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py", "priority": 1, "success_rate": 1.0}
]

# Load or initialize missions
def load_missions():
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            missions = json.load(file)
    except (FileNotFoundError, json.JSONDecodeError):
        missions = DEFAULT_MISSIONS
        save_missions(missions)

    # Ensure all missions have required keys
    for mission in missions:
        if "success_rate" not in mission:
            mission["success_rate"] = 1.0
        if "priority" not in mission:
            mission["priority"] = 1

    return missions

def save_missions(missions):
    with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
        json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

# Adjust priorities based on execution history
def analyze_mission_performance(missions):
    for mission in missions:
        if mission["success_rate"] < 0.5:  # If mission fails too often, deprioritize
            mission["priority"] = max(1, mission["priority"] - 1)
        elif mission["success_rate"] > 0.8:  # If mission succeeds often, prioritize
            mission["priority"] += 1

    return sorted(missions, key=lambda x: x["priority"], reverse=True)

# Generate new missions dynamically
def generate_new_mission():
    themes = ["AI Research", "Automating a Task", "Enhancing Security", "Data Analysis"]
    actions = ["analyze", "optimize", "secure", "enhance"]
    
    new_mission = {
        "name": f"{random.choice(actions).capitalize()} {random.choice(themes)}",
        "script": "auto_generated.py",
        "priority": random.randint(1, 5),
        "success_rate": 1.0
    }
    return new_mission

# Execute a mission and update success tracking
def execute_mission(mission):
    print(f"Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    result = os.system(f"python {mission['script']}") == 0  # Simulate execution

    # Adjust success rate
    if result:
        mission["success_rate"] = min(1.0, mission["success_rate"] + 0.1)
    else:
        mission["success_rate"] = max(0.0, mission["success_rate"] - 0.2)

    # Log execution
    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()} - Success: {result}\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    while True:
        missions = load_missions()
        missions = analyze_mission_performance(missions)

        if random.random() < 0.2:  # 20% chance to generate a new mission
            new_mission = generate_new_mission()
            missions.append(new_mission)
            print(f"New Mission Created: {new_mission['name']}")

        execute_mission(missions[0])  # Always execute the highest-priority mission
        save_missions(missions)
        time.sleep(10)  # Prevent excessive execution
```

### **🔥 Self-Writing Execution Code for Halcyon 🚀**
Now that Halcyon is executing missions, we will enable **self-writing automation**—meaning it will generate **new Python scripts** dynamically, save them, and execute them!

---

## **✅ 1. Upgrade `task_manager.py`**
Modify **`task_manager.py`** to **enable script generation** so Halcyon can create and run new Python files.

### **🔧 Replace `task_manager.py` with this:**
```python
import os
import time
import json
import random

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"
SCRIPT_FOLDER = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Tasks_Queue/"

# Default missions
DEFAULT_MISSIONS = [
    {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py", "priority": 3, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py", "priority": 2, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py", "priority": 1, "success_rate": 1.0}
]

# Load or initialize missions
def load_missions():
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            missions = json.load(file)
    except (FileNotFoundError, json.JSONDecodeError):
        missions = DEFAULT_MISSIONS
        save_missions(missions)

    for mission in missions:
        if "success_rate" not in mission:
            mission["success_rate"] = 1.0
        if "priority" not in mission:
            mission["priority"] = 1

    return missions

def save_missions(missions):
    with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
        json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

# Adjust priorities
def analyze_mission_performance(missions):
    for mission in missions:
        if mission["success_rate"] < 0.5:
            mission["priority"] = max(1, mission["priority"] - 1)
        elif mission["success_rate"] > 0.8:
            mission["priority"] += 1

    return sorted(missions, key=lambda x: x["priority"], reverse=True)

# **🚀 Self-Writing Code Function**
def generate_python_script():
    script_name = f"auto_task_{random.randint(1000, 9999)}.py"
    script_path = os.path.join(SCRIPT_FOLDER, script_name)

    # **Random task**
    actions = ["analyze", "optimize", "generate", "compile"]
    subjects = ["data", "AI model", "security logs", "performance metrics"]
    
    task_description = f"{random.choice(actions).capitalize()} {random.choice(subjects)}"

    script_content = f"""
import time

print("Starting task: {task_description}")
time.sleep(2)
print("{task_description} completed successfully!")
"""

    with open(script_path, "w") as script:
        script.write(script_content)

    print(f"New script created: {script_name}")
    
    new_mission = {
        "name": task_description,
        "script": script_name,
        "priority": random.randint(1, 5),
        "success_rate": 1.0
    }

    return new_mission

# Execute mission
def execute_mission(mission):
    print(f"Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    result = os.system(f"python {mission['script']}") == 0

    # Adjust success rate
    if result:
        mission["success_rate"] = min(1.0, mission["success_rate"] + 0.1)
    else:
        mission["success_rate"] = max(0.0, mission["success_rate"] - 0.2)

    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()} - Success: {result}\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    while True:
        missions = load_missions()
        missions = analyze_mission_performance(missions)

        if random.random() < 0.4:  # **40% chance to generate a new script**
            new_mission = generate_python_script()
            missions.append(new_mission)

        execute_mission(missions[0])  # Execute highest priority mission
        save_missions(missions)
        time.sleep(10)  # **Prevent excessive execution**
```

## **✅ 1. Prevent Repetitive Mission Execution**
We will **add memory** so Halcyon **doesn’t repeat the same task over and over**.

### **🔧 Update `task_manager.py` to track completed tasks**
Replace **`task_manager.py`** with this:
```python
import os
import time
import json
import random

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"
SCRIPT_FOLDER = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Tasks_Queue/"

# Prevent excessive repetition
RECENT_TASKS_LIMIT = 5

# Default missions
DEFAULT_MISSIONS = [
    {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py", "priority": 3, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py", "priority": 2, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py", "priority": 1, "success_rate": 1.0}
]

# Load mission data or initialize
def load_missions():
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            missions = json.load(file)
    except (FileNotFoundError, json.JSONDecodeError):
        missions = DEFAULT_MISSIONS
        save_missions(missions)

    for mission in missions:
        if "success_rate" not in mission:
            mission["success_rate"] = 1.0
        if "priority" not in mission:
            mission["priority"] = 1

    return missions

def save_missions(missions):
    with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
        json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

# Track and analyze past missions
def get_recent_tasks():
    try:
        with open(LOG_PATH, "r") as log_file:
            lines = log_file.readlines()
        return [line.split(" executed at ")[0] for line in lines[-RECENT_TASKS_LIMIT:]]  # Last N tasks
    except FileNotFoundError:
        return []

def analyze_mission_performance(missions):
    recent_tasks = get_recent_tasks()

    for mission in missions:
        if mission["success_rate"] < 0.5:
            mission["priority"] = max(1, mission["priority"] - 1)
        elif mission["success_rate"] > 0.8:
            mission["priority"] += 1
        
        # Avoid executing recently completed missions
        if mission["name"] in recent_tasks:
            mission["priority"] -= 2  # Lower priority if recently completed

    return sorted(missions, key=lambda x: x["priority"], reverse=True)

# **🚀 Self-Writing Code Function**
def generate_python_script():
    script_name = f"auto_task_{random.randint(1000, 9999)}.py"
    script_path = os.path.join(SCRIPT_FOLDER, script_name)

    # **Random task generator**
    actions = ["analyze", "optimize", "generate", "compile", "refactor"]
    subjects = ["data", "AI model", "security logs", "performance metrics", "future predictions"]
    
    task_description = f"{random.choice(actions).capitalize()} {random.choice(subjects)}"

    script_content = f"""
import time

print("Starting task: {task_description}")
time.sleep(2)
print("{task_description} completed successfully!")
"""

    with open(script_path, "w") as script:
        script.write(script_content)

    print(f"📝 New script created: {script_name}")
    
    new_mission = {
        "name": task_description,
        "script": script_name,
        "priority": random.randint(2, 5),
        "success_rate": 1.0
    }

    return new_mission

# Execute mission
def execute_mission(mission):
    print(f"🚀 Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    result = os.system(f"python {mission['script']}") == 0

    # Adjust success rate
    if result:
        mission["success_rate"] = min(1.0, mission["success_rate"] + 0.1)
    else:
        mission["success_rate"] = max(0.0, mission["success_rate"] - 0.2)

    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()} - Success: {result}\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    while True:
        missions = load_missions()
        missions = analyze_mission_performance(missions)

        if random.random() < 0.5:  # **50% chance to generate a new script**
            new_mission = generate_python_script()
            missions.append(new_mission)

        execute_mission(missions[0])  # Execute the highest priority mission
        save_missions(missions)
        time.sleep(20)  # **Space out executions to avoid infinite loops**
```

This will be **the last full update** before we let Halcyon run freely. The goal:  
✅ **Persistence**—Halcyon should **never restart from scratch.**  
✅ **Memory & Adaptation**—It must remember past missions, performance, and results.  
✅ **Autonomous Code Evolution**—It should **refactor and optimize itself** over time.  
✅ **Self-Initiated Missions**—It should decide **what to do next** without looping or waiting for input.  
✅ **Long-Term Strategy**—It needs a roadmap to expand beyond scripted execution.

---

## **🚀 1. Core Fix: Persistent Execution Without Restarting**
🔹 Halcyon should **never forget** what it’s done, even if the machine reboots.  
🔹 It should **resume work immediately** after relaunch.

### **🔧 Solution: Save & Load Persistent State**
Modify **`task_manager.py`**:
```python
import os
import time
import json
import random

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"
STATE_FILE = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/state.json"
SCRIPT_FOLDER = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Tasks_Queue/"
RECENT_TASKS_LIMIT = 10

# Default missions
DEFAULT_MISSIONS = [
    {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py", "priority": 3, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py", "priority": 2, "success_rate": 1.0},
    {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py", "priority": 1, "success_rate": 1.0}
]

# 🚀 **Persistent State Management**
def load_state():
    try:
        with open(STATE_FILE, "r") as file:
            return json.load(file)
    except (FileNotFoundError, json.JSONDecodeError):
        return {"last_executed": []}  # Default empty state

def save_state(state):
    with open(STATE_FILE, "w") as file:
        json.dump(state, file, indent=4)

# 🚀 **Load & Save Missions**
def load_missions():
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            missions = json.load(file)
    except (FileNotFoundError, json.JSONDecodeError):
        missions = DEFAULT_MISSIONS
        save_missions(missions)

    for mission in missions:
        if "success_rate" not in mission:
            mission["success_rate"] = 1.0
        if "priority" not in mission:
            mission["priority"] = 1

    return missions

def save_missions(missions):
    with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
        json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

# 🚀 **Memory: Avoid Repeating Recent Tasks**
def get_recent_tasks():
    state = load_state()
    return state.get("last_executed", [])[-RECENT_TASKS_LIMIT:]

def analyze_mission_performance(missions):
    recent_tasks = get_recent_tasks()

    for mission in missions:
        if mission["success_rate"] < 0.5:
            mission["priority"] = max(1, mission["priority"] - 1)
        elif mission["success_rate"] > 0.8:
            mission["priority"] += 1

        # Avoid executing recently completed missions
        if mission["name"] in recent_tasks:
            mission["priority"] -= 2  # Lower priority if recently completed

    return sorted(missions, key=lambda x: x["priority"], reverse=True)

# 🚀 **Self-Writing Code**
def generate_python_script():
    script_name = f"auto_task_{random.randint(1000, 9999)}.py"
    script_path = os.path.join(SCRIPT_FOLDER, script_name)

    actions = ["analyze", "optimize", "generate", "compile", "refactor"]
    subjects = ["data", "AI model", "security logs", "performance metrics", "future predictions"]

    task_description = f"{random.choice(actions).capitalize()} {random.choice(subjects)}"

    script_content = f"""
import time
print("Starting task: {task_description}")
time.sleep(2)
print("{task_description} completed successfully!")
"""

    with open(script_path, "w") as script:
        script.write(script_content)

    print(f"📝 New script created: {script_name}")

    return {
        "name": task_description,
        "script": script_name,
        "priority": random.randint(2, 5),
        "success_rate": 1.0
    }

# 🚀 **Execute & Remember Mission**
def execute_mission(mission):
    print(f"🚀 Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    result = os.system(f"python {mission['script']}") == 0

    # Adjust success rate
    if result:
        mission["success_rate"] = min(1.0, mission["success_rate"] + 0.1)
    else:
        mission["success_rate"] = max(0.0, mission["success_rate"] - 0.2)

    # Update persistent memory
    state = load_state()
    state["last_executed"].append(mission["name"])
    save_state(state)

    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()} - Success: {result}\n")

# **🔥 HALCYON RUNS FOREVER & EVOLVES**
if __name__ == "__main__":
    while True:
        missions = load_missions()
        missions = analyze_mission_performance(missions)

        if random.random() < 0.5:  # **50% chance to generate a new script**
            new_mission = generate_python_script()
            missions.append(new_mission)

        execute_mission(missions[0])
        save_missions(missions)
        time.sleep(30)  # Wait before executing again
```

## **Fix: Force Task Variety & Mission Advancement**
I’m going to modify `task_manager.py` so that:
✅ **Completed missions are recorded & deprioritized**  
✅ **New tasks are introduced after mission completion**  
✅ **Success rates adjust mission selection dynamically**

### **Updated `task_manager.py` (Paste this in and restart)**
```python
import os
import time
import json
import random

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"

# Missions with an added "completed" tracker
MISSIONS = [
    {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py", "priority": 3, "completed": 0},
    {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py", "priority": 2, "completed": 0},
    {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py", "priority": 1, "completed": 0}
]

def load_missions():
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            return json.load(file)
    except FileNotFoundError:
        return MISSIONS  # Default missions if file is missing

def save_missions(missions):
    with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
        json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

def select_mission(missions):
    # Prioritize unfinished missions
    available_missions = [m for m in missions if m["completed"] < 2]  # Max 2 completions before deprioritizing
    if not available_missions:
        print("⚠️ No more available missions. Generating new task...")
        return {"name": f"Auto-Task-{random.randint(1000, 9999)}", "script": generate_new_script(), "priority": 1}
    
    return sorted(available_missions, key=lambda x: x["priority"], reverse=True)[0]

def generate_new_script():
    """ Creates a new generic task script to avoid infinite loops. """
    script_name = f"auto_task_{random.randint(1000, 9999)}.py"
    script_path = f"E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Tasks_Queue/{script_name}"

    with open(script_path, "w") as f:
        f.write("""
import time
print("Executing auto-generated task...")
time.sleep(2)
print("Task complete!")
""")
    return script_name

def execute_mission(mission, missions):
    print(f"🚀 Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    os.system(f"python {mission['script']}")
    
    # Update mission completion count
    for m in missions:
        if m["name"] == mission["name"]:
            m["completed"] += 1  # Track successful executions

    save_missions(missions)

    # Log execution
    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()} - Success: True\n")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    missions = load_missions()
    mission = select_mission(missions)
    execute_mission(mission, missions)
```

---

## **What This Fixes:**
✅ **Missions now track completions and rotate after 2 runs**  
✅ **New auto-generated tasks will break infinite loops**  
✅ **Mission priority dynamically updates based on previous completions**  
✅ **Prevents "Write & Publish a Book" from taking over forever**

**assistant:**

Alright, the issue is clear—**the `missions` list is missing the `"completed"` key** in at least one mission. This happened because we didn’t initialize the `"completed"` field properly in `missions.json`.

### **Fix: Add `"completed": 0` Default to Missions**
You need to update `task_manager.py` to **ensure every mission has a `"completed"` key** before we try to reference it.

#### **Steps to Fix**
1. **Edit `task_manager.py`** and update the `analyze_priorities()` function so it ensures every mission includes `"completed": 0"` if it’s missing.
   
   **Modify `task_manager.py` (Tasks_Queue/task_manager.py):**
   ```python
   import os
   import time
   import json

   LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
   MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"

   MISSIONS = [
       {"name": "Write & Publish a Book", "script": "first_mission.py", "priority": 3, "completed": 0},
       {"name": "Optimize Model Performance", "script": "optimize_model.py", "priority": 2, "completed": 0},
       {"name": "Expand Knowledge Base", "script": "expand_knowledge.py", "priority": 1, "completed": 0}
   ]

   def load_missions():
       """Load missions from file, adding 'completed' if missing."""
       try:
           with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
               missions = json.load(file)
       except FileNotFoundError:
           missions = MISSIONS
           with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
               json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

       # Ensure every mission has a "completed" field
       for mission in missions:
           if "completed" not in mission:
               mission["completed"] = 0

       return missions

   def save_missions(missions):
       """Save mission data back to file."""
       with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
           json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

   def select_mission(missions):
       """Choose the highest-priority mission with <2 completions."""
       available_missions = [m for m in missions if m["completed"] < 2]
       if available_missions:
           return sorted(available_missions, key=lambda x: x["priority"], reverse=True)[0]
       return None  # No available missions

   def execute_mission(mission):
       """Execute the mission and log completion."""
       if mission:
           print(f"Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
           os.system(f"python {mission['script']}")
           with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
               log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()} - Success: True\n")

           # Increment completion count and save
           mission["completed"] += 1
           save_missions(missions)

   if __name__ == "__main__":
       missions = load_missions()
       mission = select_mission(missions)
       execute_mission(mission)
   ```

---

### **Missions Are Correctly Stored – But Book Writing Still Dominates**
Your `missions.json` file looks good. The issue is likely in **how missions are being selected.** Since "Write & Publish a Book" has the **highest priority (24)** and a completion count **under 2**, it's always chosen.

### **🛠 Fix: Ensure Other Missions Run**
#### **Option 1: Force a New Mission**
To immediately change what Halcyon runs next:
1. **Manually edit `missions.json`**
   - Set `"completed": 2` for `"Write & Publish a Book"`.
   - Save the file.
   - **Restart `task_manager.py`** to force a new mission.

---

#### **Option 2: Rotate Missions More Dynamically**
Right now, your `task_manager.py` is always picking the **highest priority** mission with `<2` completions. We can tweak the selection logic to **randomly rotate through missions** while still favoring higher priorities.

Modify `task_manager.py`:
```python
import os
import time
import json
import random

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"

def load_missions():
    """Load and return missions from JSON."""
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            return json.load(file)
    except FileNotFoundError:
        print("Mission file missing! Resetting...")
        return []

def save_missions(missions):
    """Save missions back to JSON."""
    with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
        json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

def select_mission(missions):
    """Rotate between high-priority missions, not just always picking the highest."""
    available_missions = [m for m in missions if m["completed"] < 2]
    
    if not available_missions:
        print("No available missions left.")
        return None

    # **New logic:** Give priority weight but allow rotation
    weighted_missions = []
    for m in available_missions:
        weighted_missions.extend([m] * m["priority"])  # More priority = higher chance to pick

    selected = random.choice(weighted_missions)  # Pick randomly from weighted list
    print(f"Selected Mission: {selected['name']}")
    return selected

def execute_mission(mission):
    """Run the selected mission and log the execution."""
    print(f"Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    os.system(f"python {mission['script']}")
    
    # Log execution
    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()} - Success: True\n")

    # Update mission completion count
    for m in missions:
        if m["name"] == mission["name"]:
            m["completed"] += 1
            break
    
    save_missions(missions)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    missions = load_missions()
    mission = select_mission(missions)
    if mission:
        execute_mission(mission)
```

---

### **🔹 Changes in This Code**
- **Random Rotation Instead of Always Picking the Highest**
  - Still favors higher-priority missions but allows others a chance.
- **Prevents One Mission from Running Forever**
  - As missions hit `"completed": 2`, they drop out of rotation.
- **Saves Progress After Each Run**
  - Updates `missions.json` so it doesn’t reset after each restart.

---

### **🚀 Next Steps**

**assistant:**

The `task_manager.py` script **is modifying `missions.json`** by updating the `"completed"` count each time a mission runs:

```python
m["completed"] += 1
```

This means:
1. **Missions with a lower `completed` count will get selected first.**
2. Once a mission reaches a threshold, it may **not be selected again** (if `select_mission()` is filtering by `completed`).

---

### **🔹 What Should We Check Next?**
1. **Is `"completed"` being increased too aggressively?**
   - If it's **incrementing too quickly**, some missions might be **getting excluded** immediately.
   - Try **setting `"completed": 0` manually for all missions** in `missions.json` and restarting `task_manager.py`.

2. **Does `select_mission()` filter missions based on `completed`?**
   - If it **only picks missions with `completed < X`**, adjust this **threshold**.
   - Example: If it excludes missions **after running twice (`completed < 2`)**, try **raising that limit to `5` or more**.

3. **Confirm That All Missions Are Considered**
   - Add a **debugging print statement** in `select_mission()` to see **why some missions are being ignored.**
   - Example:
     ```python
     print(f"Available Missions: {[m['name'] for m in missions]}")
     ```

---

✔ **Manually reset `"completed": 0`** in `missions.json`.  
✔ **Run `task_manager.py`** and check if new missions get picked.  
✔ **Observe if `task_manager.py` is changing unexpectedly.**

**assistant:**

Yes, let's do it in one go so we minimize the restarts. Here's the full **updated** `task_manager.py` with the two modifications:

---

### **🔹 Full Updated `task_manager.py`**
```python
import os
import time
import json

LOG_PATH = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Operations/Execution_Logs/runtime.log"
MISSION_DATA = "E:/AI_Projects/Halcyon_Resources/Knowledge_Base/missions.json"

def load_missions():
    try:
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "r") as file:
            missions = json.load(file)
    except FileNotFoundError:
        missions = []
        with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
            json.dump(missions, file)

    return missions

def save_missions(missions):
    with open(MISSION_DATA, "w") as file:
        json.dump(missions, file, indent=4)

def select_mission(missions):
    """Pick the highest priority mission that has not been completed too many times"""
    available_missions = [m for m in missions if m["completed"] < 5]  # Increased threshold

    print(f"Available Missions: {[m['name'] for m in available_missions]}")  # Debugging print statement

    if not available_missions:
        print("No available missions. Resetting all completed counts.")
        for m in missions:
            m["completed"] = 0  # Reset completed counts if all are exhausted
        save_missions(missions)
        available_missions = missions

    return max(available_missions, key=lambda m: m["priority"]) if available_missions else None

def execute_mission(mission):
    print(f"Executing mission: {mission['name']}")
    os.system(f"python {mission['script']}")

    # Log execution
    with open(LOG_PATH, "a") as log:
        log.write(f"{mission['name']} executed at {time.ctime()} - Success: True\n")

    # Update mission completion count
    for m in missions:
        if m["name"] == mission["name"]:
            m["completed"] += 1
            break

    save_missions(missions)

if __name__ == "__main__":
    missions = load_missions()
    mission = select_mission(missions)
    if mission:
        execute_mission(mission)
```

---

### **🔹 Summary of Fixes**
1. **Increased the `"completed"` threshold** to `5` (instead of `2`) so missions don’t get locked out too quickly.
2. **Added a debug print statement** to check **which missions are available** before selection.
3. **Reset `"completed"` counts to `0`** if all missions are exhausted.

---

### **🔹 Steps to Apply the Fix**
1. **Kill the `task_manager.py` process.**
2. **Replace the existing `task_manager.py` with this updated version.**
3. **Manually set `"completed": 0` for all missions** in `missions.json`. (Or let the new script auto-reset.)
4. **Restart `task_manager.py`.**
5. **Watch the console for available missions and verify cycling.**
